10.098 10.098 0 0 1 9.123-13.142V4.645a1 1 0 0 1 1.621-.784"></path></svg></button></div></div></aside><div class="col-lg-8 col-sm-12"><nav><h2 class="mc-text-h4">Jump To Section</h2><ul class="mc-mt-3"><li class="mc-mt-3"><a class="mc-text--link" href="#4OwfDU4UkffrE0jncocL3K">18 Common Fantasy Subgenres</a></li><li class="mc-mt-3"><a class="mc-text--link" href="#4iKhu3Oz9NpLTUibeM0gUl">Want to Learn More About Writing?</a></li></ul></nav><hr class="mc-separator mc-my-10 mc-separator--subtle" aria-hidden="true"/><section><div class="mc-pb-6 mc-mst-12" id="4OwfDU4UkffrE0jncocL3K"><h2 class="mc-text-h2 highlight-shareable">18 Common Fantasy Subgenres</h2><div class="mc-text-large mc-mt-4 highlight-shareable"><p class="mc-mb-6">Fantasy novels take on many forms, and the number of distinct fantasy subgenres seems to grow with each passing year. Here are 18 particularly important subgenres within the world of fantasy:</p><ol class="mc-m-4"><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">1.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Dystopian fantasy</strong>: Sometimes grouped in with science fiction, <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction","linkCopy":"speculative fiction","category":null}'>speculative fiction</a>, and literary fiction, dystopian fantasies imagine worlds gone wrong. The settings are at once familiar to contemporary audiences and also alarmingly worse than the present world. Jack Vances <em class="mc-text--italic">Dying Earth</em> series is a pulpy example of this subgenre of fantasy fiction. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">2.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">High fantasy</strong>: Sometimes called epic fantasy, high fantasy is set in a magical environment that has its own rules and physical laws. This subgenres plots and themes have a grand scale and typically center on a single, well-developed hero or a band of heroes, such as Frodo Baggins and his cohorts in J.R.R. Tolkiens <em class="mc-text--italic">The Lord of the Rings</em> or Bilbo Baggins and the dwarves in <em class="mc-text--italic">The Hobbit</em>. George R.R. Martin combines high fantasy with elements of medieval fantasy and romance in his <em class="mc-text--italic">Song of Ice and Fire</em> series (and the <em class="mc-text--italic">Game of Thrones</em> television series based upon those books). </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">3.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Low fantasy</strong>: Set in the real world, low fantasy includes unexpected magical elements that surprise ordinary characters, like the plastic figurines come to life in Lynne Reid Bankss <em class="mc-text--italic">The Indian in the Cupboard</em>. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">4.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Magical realism</strong>: While similar to low fantasy, magical realism characters accept fantastical elements like levitation and telekinesis as a normal part of their otherwise realistic world, as in Gabriel Garca Mrquezs magical realism classic <em class="mc-text--italic">One Hundred Years of Solitude</em>. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">5.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Sword and sorcery</strong>: A subset of high fantasy, this subgenre focuses on sword-wielding heroessuch as the titular barbarian in Robert E. Howards <em class="mc-text--italic">Conan</em> pulp fiction storiesas well as magic or witchcraft. J.K. Rowling popularized the sword and sorcery subgenre for young adults with her <em class="mc-text--italic">Harry Potter</em> series. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">6.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Urban fantasy</strong>: <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre","linkCopy":"Urban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories","category":null}'>Urban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories</a> in which fantastical characters and concepts are placed in a real world urban setting, often in the present day. Urban fantasy novels have devoted followings and they have spawned film and TV adaptations. Urban fantasy stories often draw from noir and gritty police procedurals. They also may incorporate fantastical elements and supernatural creatures. These could involve undead zombies, vampires, druids, demons, wizardry, witchcraft, and other such fantasy tropes. <em class="mc-text--italic">The Dresden Files</em> by Jim Butcher is an example of urban fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">7.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Paranormal romance</strong>: This fantasy subgenre combines romantic themes with fantasy elements like vampires, werewolves, shifters, faeries, and zombie armies. Many contemporary fantasy series blur the line between urban fantasy stories, coming-of-age tales, and paranormal romances. Patricia Briggs and Jeaniene Frost are popular authors in this subgenre. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">8.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Dark fantasy</strong>: Combining elements of fantasy with the horror genre, dark fantasys aim is to unnerve and frighten readers. For example, consider the gargantuan, <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories","linkCopy":"otherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe","category":null}'>otherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe</a>. Gothic and Victorian dark fantasy tends to embrace a paranormal setting and supernatural elements, which can range from vampires to werewolves and beyond. Note that by no means is every paranormal fantasy a dark fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">9.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Grimdark fantasy</strong>: One step beyond dark fantasy, grimdark novels pry into the blackest depths of the human condition, often in the proverbial underbelly of an alternate world. <em class="mc-text--italic">The Court of Broken Knives</em> by Anna Smith Spark is a popular book within this subgenre. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">10.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Fables</strong>: Using personified animals and the supernatural, fables impart moral lessons, like the stories in <em class="mc-text--italic">Aesops Fables</em> and <em class="mc-text--italic">Arabian Nights</em>. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">11.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Fairy Tales</strong>: <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts","linkCopy":"Intended for children, fairy tales","category":null}'>Intended for children, fairy tales</a> and folk tales are typically set in distant magical worlds (with beginnings like Once upon a time, in a land far, far away) where trolls, dragons, witches, and other supernatural characters are an accepted truth, as in the Brothers Grimms Grimms Fairy Tales. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">12.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Superhero fantasy</strong>: Unlike stories in which a hero acquires special abilities through scientific means, such as exposure to radiation, the protagonists powers in more fantastical superhero stories are supernatural. Many superhero stories are set in a low fantasy worldone thats quite similar to our own world. Superheroes ranging from Wonder Woman to Thor bring fantasy elements to worlds that otherwise obey the known laws of science. Many superhero fantasy authors have worked in the comic book medium, from Stan Lee to Bob Kane. As such, superhero fiction in the fantasy genre is also known as comic fantasy or comic book fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">13.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Fantasy of manners</strong>: This subgenre, exemplified by fantasy books like <em class="mc-text--italic">Gormenghast</em> by Mervyn Peake, combines supernatural world-building with the type of society-centric concerns one might encounter in a work by Edith Wharton or Noel Coward. Human drama and pettiness may outweigh magical powers in this subgenre of fantasy literature. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">14.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Crossworlds fantasy</strong>: Sometimes called portal fantasy, this subgenre involves characters transporting from a normal world to a magical one. This requires authors to engage in both magical world-building and grounded realistic world-building. Crossworlds fantasy stories often appeal to children, as seen in the <em class="mc-text--italic">Chronicles of Narnia</em> series by C.S. Lewis and <em class="mc-text--italic">Alice in Wonderland</em> by Lewis Carroll. These works also fit a category known as juvenile fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">15.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Steampunk fantasy</strong>: This highly specific subgenre combines the Victorian science and technology of the Industrial Revolution with contemporary takes on robots and machines. As such, steampunk fantasy is at once alternate history, science fantasy, and a modern fantasyalthough the specifics vary with specific novels. <em class="mc-text--italic">Soulless</em> by Gail Carriger is a particularly well-regarded steampunk fantasy novel. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">16.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Arthurian fantasy</strong>: These historical fantasy stories exist in a magical world of King Arthur, although Arthur himself is not always the main character. Due to their magical setting, Arthurian fantasy novels and short stories tend to feature mythic creatures like dragons, and many of their heroes are knightswhich also makes them part of the heroic fantasy subgenre. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">17.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Sci-fi fantasy</strong>: These stories can be set in any variety of time periodswhich means they can be a contemporary fantasy, a modern fantasy, a futuristic fantasy, or even historical fantasybut they establish a new world where scientific advancements have changed the rules of engagement, while still incorporating magical elements. The <em class="mc-text--italic">Star Wars</em> series and the various works of Isaac Asimov have helped set the bar for sci-fi fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">18.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Wuxia fantasy</strong>: This subgenre is rooted in classic Chinese literature. It involves elements of fantasy interspersed with martial arts. <em class="mc-text--italic">Jade City</em> by Fonda Lee is an example of wuxia fantasy. </li></ol></div></div><div class="mc-pb-6 mc-mst-12" id="4iKhu3Oz9NpLTUibeM0gUl"><h2 class="mc-text-h2 highlight-shareable">Want to Learn More About Writing?</h2><div class="mc-text-large mc-mt-4 highlight-shareable"><p class="mc-mb-6">Become a better writer with the <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/","linkCopy":"Masterclass Annual Membership","category":null}'>Masterclass Annual Membership</a>. Gain access to exclusive video lessons taught by literary masters, including David Baldacci, Joyce Carol Oates, Dan Brown, Margaret Atwood, James Patterson, David Sedaris, and more.</p></div></div></section></div><div class="col-3 d-none d-lg-flex flex-column justify-content-evenly"></div></div></section></div><div id="next-sticky-container" class="bottom d="M47.6851 14.7617C47.6533 14.41 47.6914 14.0552 47.797 13.72C47.9026 13.3849 48.0734 13.0767 48.2984 12.8153C48.5234 12.5539 48.7977 12.345 49.1037 12.2021C49.4096 12.0592 49.7405 11.9854 50.075 Understanding the different fantasy subgenres can help aspiring writers find their niche so that they can create a fantasy series that readers can enjoy for years to come. \n","readTime":345,"articleStructuredData":[{"@context":"http://schema.org","@type":"Article","publisher":{"@context":"http://schema.org","@type":"Organization","brand":"MasterClass","name":"MasterClass","url":"http://www.masterclass.com","logo":{"@type":"ImageObject","url":"https://www.masterclass.com/favicon-194x194.png","name":"MasterClass Logo","width":"194","height":"194"},"address":"475 Brannan St Ste 220, San Francisco, CA 94107","email":"support@masterclass.com","contactPoint":[{"@type":"ContactPoint","telephone":"+1 (855) 981-8208","contactType":"customer service"}]},"name":"A Complete Overview of 18 Fantasy Subgenres","headline":"A Complete Overview of 18 Fantasy Subgenres","description":"The broad tent of fantasy literature has spawned many fantasy subgenres that range from mythical and gritty to modern and otherworldly. Understanding the different fantasy subgenres can help aspiring writers find their niche so that they can create a fantasy series that readers can enjoy for years to come. \n","datePublished":"2020-01-13 14:37:49 -0800","dateModified":"2021-08-06 08:44:26 -0700","articleBody":"Fantasy novels take on many forms, and the number of distinct fantasy subgenres seems to grow with each passing year. Here are 18 particularly important subgenres within the world of fantasy:\n\n1. __Dystopian fantasy__: Sometimes grouped in with science fiction, [speculative fiction](https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction), and literary fiction, dystopian fantasies imagine worlds gone wrong. The settings are at once familiar to contemporary audiences and also alarmingly worse than the present world. Jack Vances *Dying Earth* series is a pulpy example of this subgenre of fantasy fiction.\n2. __High fantasy__: Sometimes called epic fantasy, high fantasy is set in a magical environment that has its own rules and physical laws. This subgenres plots and themes have a grand scale and typically center on a single, well-developed hero or a band of heroes, such as Frodo Baggins and his cohorts in J.R.R. Tolkiens *The Lord of the Rings* or Bilbo Baggins and the dwarves in *The Hobbit*. George R.R. Martin combines high fantasy with elements of medieval fantasy and romance in his *Song of Ice and Fire* series (and the *Game of Thrones* television series based upon those books).\n3. __Low fantasy__: Set in the real world, low fantasy includes unexpected magical elements that surprise ordinary characters, like the plastic figurines come to life in Lynne Reid Bankss *The Indian in the Cupboard*.\n4. __Magical realism__: While similar to low fantasy, magical realism characters accept fantastical elements like levitation and telekinesis as a normal part of their otherwise realistic world, as in Gabriel Garca Mrquezs magical realism classic *One Hundred Years of Solitude*.\n5. __Sword and sorcery__: A subset of high fantasy, this subgenre focuses on sword-wielding heroessuch as the titular barbarian in Robert E. Howards *Conan* pulp fiction storiesas well as magic or witchcraft. J.K. Rowling popularized the sword and sorcery subgenre for young adults with her *Harry Potter* series.\n6. __Urban fantasy__: [Urban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories](https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre) in which fantastical characters and concepts are placed in a real world urban setting, often in the present day. Urban fantasy novels have devoted followings and they have spawned film and TV adaptations. Urban fantasy stories often draw from noir and gritty police procedurals. They also may incorporate fantastical elements and supernatural creatures. These could involve undead zombies, vampires, druids, demons, wizardry, witchcraft, and other such fantasy tropes. *The Dresden Files* by Jim Butcher is an example of urban fantasy.\n7. __Paranormal romance__: This fantasy subgenre combines romantic themes with fantasy elements like vampires, werewolves, shifters, faeries, and zombie armies. Many contemporary fantasy series blur the line between urban fantasy stories, coming-of-age tales, and paranormal romances. Patricia Briggs and Jeaniene Frost are popular authors in this subgenre.\n8. __Dark fantasy__: Combining elements of fantasy with the horror genre, dark fantasys aim is to unnerve and frighten readers. For example, consider the gargantuan, [otherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe](https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories). Gothic and Victorian dark fantasy tends to embrace a paranormal setting and supernatural elements, which can range from vampires to werewolves and beyond. Note that by no means is every paranormal fantasy a dark fantasy.\n9. __Grimdark fantasy__: One step beyond dark fantasy, grimdark novels pry into the blackest depths of the human condition, often in the proverbial underbelly of an alternate world. *The Court of Broken Knives* by Anna Smith Spark is a popular book within this subgenre.\n10. __Fables__: Using personified animals and the supernatural, fables impart moral lessons, like the stories in *Aesops Fables* and *Arabian Nights*.\n11. __Fairy Tales__: [Intended for children, fairy tales](https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts) and folk tales are typically set in distant magical worlds (with beginnings like Once upon a time, in a land far, far away) where trolls, dragons, witches, and other supernatural characters are an accepted truth, as in the Brothers Grimms Grimms Fairy Tales.\n12. __Superhero fantasy__: Unlike stories in which a hero acquires special abilities through scientific means, such as exposure to radiation, the protagonists powers in more fantastical superhero stories are supernatural. Many superhero stories are set in a low fantasy worldone thats quite similar to our own world. Superheroes ranging from Wonder Woman to Thor bring fantasy elements to worlds that otherwise obey the known laws of science. Many superhero fantasy authors have worked in the comic book medium, from Stan Lee to Bob Kane. As such, superhero fiction in the fantasy genre is also known as comic fantasy or comic book fantasy.\n13. __Fantasy of manners__: This subgenre, exemplified by fantasy books like *Gormenghast* by Mervyn Peake, combines supernatural world-building with the type of society-centric concerns one might encounter in a work by Edith Wharton or Noel Coward. Human drama and pettiness may outweigh magical powers in this subgenre of fantasy literature.\n14. __Crossworlds fantasy__: Sometimes called portal fantasy, this subgenre involves characters transporting from a normal world to a magical one. This requires authors to engage in both magical world-building and grounded realistic world-building. Crossworlds fantasy stories often appeal to children, as seen in the *Chronicles of Narnia* series by C.S. Lewis and *Alice in Wonderland* by Lewis Carroll. These works also fit a category known as juvenile fantasy.\n15. __Steampunk fantasy__: This highly specific subgenre combines the Victorian science and technology of the Industrial Revolution with contemporary takes on robots and machines. As such, steampunk fantasy is at once alternate history, science fantasy, and a modern fantasyalthough the specifics vary with specific novels. *Soulless* by Gail Carriger is a particularly well-regarded steampunk fantasy novel.\n16. __Arthurian fantasy__: These historical fantasy stories exist in a magical world of King Arthur, although Arthur himself is not always the main character. Due to their magical setting, Arthurian fantasy novels and short stories tend to feature mythic creatures like dragons, and many of their heroes are knightswhich also makes them part of the heroic fantasy subgenre.\n17. __Sci-fi fantasy__: These stories can be set in any variety of time periodswhich means they can be a contemporary fantasy, a modern fantasy, a futuristic fantasy, or even historical fantasybut they establish a new world where scientific advancements have changed the rules of engagement, while still incorporating magical elements. The *Star Wars* series and the various works of Isaac Asimov have helped set the bar for sci-fi fantasy.\n18. __Wuxia fantasy__: This subgenre is rooted in classic Chinese literature. It involves elements of fantasy interspersed with martial arts. *Jade City* by Fonda Lee is an example of wuxia fantasy.\n\nBecome a better writer with the [Masterclass Annual Membership](https://www.masterclass.com/). Gain access to exclusive video lessons taught by literary masters, including David Baldacci, Joyce Carol Oates, Dan Brown, Margaret Atwood, James Patterson, David Sedaris, and more.\nThe broad tent of fantasy literature has spawned many fantasy subgenres that range from mythical and gritty to modern and otherworldly. Understanding the different fantasy subgenres can help aspiring writers find their niche so that they can create a fantasy series that readers can enjoy for years to come. \n","mainEntityOfPage":{"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/a-complete-overview-of-fantasy-subgenres"},"author":{"@type":"Person","name":"MasterClass"},"image":["https://images.ctfassets.net/3s5io6mnxfqz/4eHYWk9lOVoovZaYsd6EPt/39dd332a5f875a71d86a371e0db88e63/AdobeStock_295790060.jpeg"]}],"articleSubsections":[{"id":"4OwfDU4UkffrE0jncocL3K","title":"18 Common Fantasy Subgenres","videoId":null,"entityType":"subSection","servingSize":null,"cookTime":null,"prepTime":null,"totalTime":null,"calories":null,"recipeCategory":null,"recipeCuisine":null,"recipeYield":null,"keywords":null,"description":"\u003cp class=\"mc-mb-6\"\u003eFantasy novels take on many forms, and the number of distinct fantasy subgenres seems to grow with each passing year. Here are 18 particularly important subgenres within the world of fantasy:\u003c/p\u003e\u003col class=\"mc-m-4\"\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e1.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eDystopian fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Sometimes grouped in with science fiction, \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction\",\"linkCopy\":\"speculative fiction\",\"category\":null}'\u003especulative fiction\u003c/a\u003e, and literary fiction, dystopian fantasies imagine worlds gone wrong. The settings are at once familiar to contemporary audiences and also alarmingly worse than the present world. Jack Vances \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eDying Earth\u003c/em\u003e series is a pulpy example of this subgenre of fantasy fiction. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e2.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eHigh fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Sometimes called epic fantasy, high fantasy is set in a magical environment that has its own rules and physical laws. This subgenres plots and themes have a grand scale and typically center on a single, well-developed hero or a band of heroes, such as Frodo Baggins and his cohorts in J.R.R. Tolkiens \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Lord of the Rings\u003c/em\u003e or Bilbo Baggins and the dwarves in \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Hobbit\u003c/em\u003e. George R.R. Martin combines high fantasy with elements of medieval fantasy and romance in his \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eSong of Ice and Fire\u003c/em\u003e series (and the \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eGame of Thrones\u003c/em\u003e television series based upon those books). \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e3.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eLow fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Set in the real world, low fantasy includes unexpected magical elements that surprise ordinary characters, like the plastic figurines come to life in Lynne Reid Bankss \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Indian in the Cupboard\u003c/em\u003e. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e4.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eMagical realism\u003c/strong\u003e: While similar to low fantasy, magical realism characters accept fantastical elements like levitation and telekinesis as a normal part of their otherwise realistic world, as in Gabriel Garca Mrquezs magical realism classic \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eOne Hundred Years of Solitude\u003c/em\u003e. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e5.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eSword and sorcery\u003c/strong\u003e: A subset of high fantasy, this subgenre focuses on sword-wielding heroessuch as the titular barbarian in Robert E. Howards \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eConan\u003c/em\u003e pulp fiction storiesas well as magic or witchcraft. J.K. Rowling popularized the sword and sorcery subgenre for young adults with her \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eHarry Potter\u003c/em\u003e series. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e6.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eUrban fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre\",\"linkCopy\":\"Urban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories\",\"category\":null}'\u003eUrban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories\u003c/a\u003e in which fantastical characters and concepts are placed in a real world urban setting, often in the present day. Urban fantasy novels have devoted followings and they have spawned film and TV adaptations. Urban fantasy stories often draw from noir and gritty police procedurals. They also may incorporate fantastical elements and supernatural creatures. These could involve undead zombies, vampires, druids, demons, wizardry, witchcraft, and other such fantasy tropes. \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Dresden Files\u003c/em\u003e by Jim Butcher is an example of urban fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e7.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eParanormal romance\u003c/strong\u003e: This fantasy subgenre combines romantic themes with fantasy elements like vampires, werewolves, shifters, faeries, and zombie armies. Many contemporary fantasy series blur the line between urban fantasy stories, coming-of-age tales, and paranormal romances. Patricia Briggs and Jeaniene Frost are popular authors in this subgenre. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e8.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eDark fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Combining elements of fantasy with the horror genre, dark fantasys aim is to unnerve and frighten readers. For example, consider the gargantuan, \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories\",\"linkCopy\":\"otherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe\",\"category\":null}'\u003eotherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe\u003c/a\u003e. Gothic and Victorian dark fantasy tends to embrace a paranormal setting and supernatural elements, which can range from vampires to werewolves and beyond. Note that by no means is every paranormal fantasy a dark fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e9.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eGrimdark fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: One step beyond dark fantasy, grimdark novels pry into the blackest depths of the human condition, often in the proverbial underbelly of an alternate world. \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Court of Broken Knives\u003c/em\u003e by Anna Smith Spark is a popular book within this subgenre. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e10.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eFables\u003c/strong\u003e: Using personified animals and the supernatural, fables impart moral lessons, like the stories in \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eAesops Fables\u003c/em\u003e and \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eArabian Nights\u003c/em\u003e. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e11.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eFairy Tales\u003c/strong\u003e: \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts\",\"linkCopy\":\"Intended for children, fairy tales\",\"category\":null}'\u003eIntended for children, fairy tales\u003c/a\u003e and folk tales are typically set in distant magical worlds (with beginnings like Once upon a time, in a land far, far away) where trolls, dragons, witches, and other supernatural characters are an accepted truth, as in the Brothers Grimms Grimms Fairy Tales. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e12.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eSuperhero fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Unlike stories in which a hero acquires special abilities through scientific means, such as exposure to radiation, the protagonists powers in more fantastical superhero stories are supernatural. Many superhero stories are set in a low fantasy worldone thats quite similar to our own world. Superheroes ranging from Wonder Woman to Thor bring fantasy elements to worlds that otherwise obey the known laws of science. Many superhero fantasy authors have worked in the comic book medium, from Stan Lee to Bob Kane. As such, superhero fiction in the fantasy genre is also known as comic fantasy or comic book fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e13.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eFantasy of manners\u003c/strong\u003e: This subgenre, exemplified by fantasy books like \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eGormenghast\u003c/em\u003e by Mervyn Peake, combines supernatural world-building with the type of society-centric concerns one might encounter in a work by Edith Wharton or Noel Coward. Human drama and pettiness may outweigh magical powers in this subgenre of fantasy literature. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e14.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eCrossworlds fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Sometimes called portal fantasy, this subgenre involves characters transporting from a normal world to a magical one. This requires authors to engage in both magical world-building and grounded realistic world-building. Crossworlds fantasy stories often appeal to children, as seen in the \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eChronicles of Narnia\u003c/em\u003e series by C.S. Lewis and \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eAlice in Wonderland\u003c/em\u003e by Lewis Carroll. These works also fit a category known as juvenile fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e15.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eSteampunk fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: This highly specific subgenre combines the Victorian science and technology of the Industrial Revolution with contemporary takes on robots and machines. As such, steampunk fantasy is at once alternate history, science fantasy, and a modern fantasyalthough the specifics vary with specific novels. \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eSoulless\u003c/em\u003e by Gail Carriger is a particularly well-regarded steampunk fantasy novel. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e16.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eArthurian fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: These historical fantasy stories exist in a magical world of King Arthur, although Arthur himself is not always the main character. Due to their magical setting, Arthurian fantasy novels and short stories tend to feature mythic creatures like dragons, and many of their heroes are knightswhich also makes them part of the heroic fantasy subgenre. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e17.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eSci-fi fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: These stories can be set in any variety of time periodswhich means they can be a contemporary fantasy, a modern fantasy, a futuristic fantasy, or even historical fantasybut they establish a new world where scientific advancements have changed the rules of engagement, while still incorporating magical elements. The \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eStar Wars\u003c/em\u003e series and the various works of Isaac Asimov have helped set the bar for sci-fi fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e18.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eWuxia fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: This subgenre is rooted in classic Chinese literature. It involves elements of fantasy interspersed with martial arts. \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eJade City\u003c/em\u003e by Fonda Lee is an example of wuxia fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e","recipeInstructions":null,"review":null,"startTime":null,"brightcoveVideoId":null,"mediaUuid":null,"recipeIngredient":null,"upNextGems":null,"mediaImageUrl":null,"mediaCaption":null},{"id":"4iKhu3Oz9NpLTUibeM0gUl","title":"Want to Learn More About Writing?","videoId":null,"entityType":"subSection","servingSize":null,"cookTime":null,"prepTime":null,"totalTime":null,"calories":null,"recipeCategory":null,"recipeCuisine":null,"recipeYield":null,"keywords":null,"description":"\u003cp class=\"mc-mb-6\"\u003eBecome a better writer with the \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/\",\"linkCopy\":\"Masterclass Annual Membership\",\"category\":null}'\u003eMasterclass Annual Membership\u003c/a\u003e. href="#4iKhu3Oz9NpLTUibeM0gUl">Want to Learn More About Writing?</a></li></ul></nav><hr class="mc-separator mc-my-10 mc-separator--subtle" aria-hidden="true"/><section><div class="mc-pb-6 mc-mst-12" id="4OwfDU4UkffrE0jncocL3K"><h2 class="mc-text-h2 highlight-shareable">18 Common Fantasy Subgenres</h2><div class="mc-text-large mc-mt-4 highlight-shareable"><p class="mc-mb-6">Fantasy novels take on many forms, and the number of distinct fantasy subgenres seems to grow with each passing year. Here are 18 particularly important subgenres within the world of fantasy:</p><ol class="mc-m-4"><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">1.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Dystopian fantasy</strong>: Sometimes grouped in with science fiction, <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction","linkCopy":"speculative fiction","category":null}'>speculative fiction</a>, and literary fiction, dystopian fantasies imagine worlds gone wrong. The settings are at once familiar to contemporary audiences and also alarmingly worse than the present world. Jack Vances <em class="mc-text--italic">Dying Earth</em> series is a pulpy example of this subgenre of fantasy fiction. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">2.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">High fantasy</strong>: Sometimes called epic fantasy, high fantasy is set in a magical environment that has its own rules and physical laws. This subgenres plots and themes have a grand scale and typically center on a single, well-developed hero or a band of heroes, such as Frodo Baggins and his cohorts in J.R.R. Tolkiens <em class="mc-text--italic">The Lord of the Rings</em> or Bilbo Baggins and the dwarves in <em class="mc-text--italic">The Hobbit</em>. George R.R. Martin combines high fantasy with elements of medieval fantasy and romance in his <em class="mc-text--italic">Song of Ice and Fire</em> series (and the <em class="mc-text--italic">Game of Thrones</em> television series based upon those books). </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">3.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Low fantasy</strong>: Set in the real world, low fantasy includes unexpected magical elements that surprise ordinary characters, like the plastic figurines come to life in Lynne Reid Bankss <em class="mc-text--italic">The Indian in the Cupboard</em>. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">4.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Magical realism</strong>: While similar to low fantasy, magical realism characters accept fantastical elements like levitation and telekinesis as a normal part of their otherwise realistic world, as in Gabriel Garca Mrquezs magical realism classic <em class="mc-text--italic">One Hundred Years of Solitude</em>. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">5.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Sword and sorcery</strong>: A subset of high fantasy, this subgenre focuses on sword-wielding heroessuch as the titular barbarian in Robert E. Howards <em class="mc-text--italic">Conan</em> pulp fiction storiesas well as magic or witchcraft. J.K. Rowling popularized the sword and sorcery subgenre for young adults with her <em class="mc-text--italic">Harry Potter</em> series. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">6.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Urban fantasy</strong>: <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre","linkCopy":"Urban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories","category":null}'>Urban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories</a> in which fantastical characters and concepts are placed in a real world urban setting, often in the present day. Urban fantasy novels have devoted followings and they have spawned film and TV adaptations. Urban fantasy stories often draw from noir and gritty police procedurals. They also may incorporate fantastical elements and supernatural creatures. These could involve undead zombies, vampires, druids, demons, wizardry, witchcraft, and other such fantasy tropes. <em class="mc-text--italic">The Dresden Files</em> by Jim Butcher is an example of urban fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">7.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Paranormal romance</strong>: This fantasy subgenre combines romantic themes with fantasy elements like vampires, werewolves, shifters, faeries, and zombie armies. Many contemporary fantasy series blur the line between urban fantasy stories, coming-of-age tales, and paranormal romances. Patricia Briggs and Jeaniene Frost are popular authors in this subgenre. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">8.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Dark fantasy</strong>: Combining elements of fantasy with the horror genre, dark fantasys aim is to unnerve and frighten readers. For example, consider the gargantuan, <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories","linkCopy":"otherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe","category":null}'>otherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe</a>. Gothic and Victorian dark fantasy tends to embrace a paranormal setting and supernatural elements, which can range from vampires to werewolves and beyond. Note that by no means is every paranormal fantasy a dark fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">9.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Grimdark fantasy</strong>: One step beyond dark fantasy, grimdark novels pry into the blackest depths of the human condition, often in the proverbial underbelly of an alternate world. <em class="mc-text--italic">The Court of Broken Knives</em> by Anna Smith Spark is a popular book within this subgenre. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">10.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Fables</strong>: Using personified animals and the supernatural, fables impart moral lessons, like the stories in <em class="mc-text--italic">Aesops Fables</em> and <em class="mc-text--italic">Arabian Nights</em>. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">11.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Fairy Tales</strong>: <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts","linkCopy":"Intended for children, fairy tales","category":null}'>Intended for children, fairy tales</a> and folk tales are typically set in distant magical worlds (with beginnings like Once upon a time, in a land far, far away) where trolls, dragons, witches, and other supernatural characters are an accepted truth, as in the Brothers Grimms Grimms Fairy Tales. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">12.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Superhero fantasy</strong>: Unlike stories in which a hero acquires special abilities through scientific means, such as exposure to radiation, the protagonists powers in more fantastical superhero stories are supernatural. Many superhero stories are set in a low fantasy worldone thats quite similar to our own world. Superheroes ranging from Wonder Woman to Thor bring fantasy elements to worlds that otherwise obey the known laws of science. Many superhero fantasy authors have worked in the comic book medium, from Stan Lee to Bob Kane. As such, superhero fiction in the fantasy genre is also known as comic fantasy or comic book fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">13.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Fantasy of manners</strong>: This subgenre, exemplified by fantasy books like <em class="mc-text--italic">Gormenghast</em> by Mervyn Peake, combines supernatural world-building with the type of society-centric concerns one might encounter in a work by Edith Wharton or Noel Coward. Human drama and pettiness may outweigh magical powers in this subgenre of fantasy literature. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">14.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Crossworlds fantasy</strong>: Sometimes called portal fantasy, this subgenre involves characters transporting from a normal world to a magical one. This requires authors to engage in both magical world-building and grounded realistic world-building. Crossworlds fantasy stories often appeal to children, as seen in the <em class="mc-text--italic">Chronicles of Narnia</em> series by C.S. Lewis and <em class="mc-text--italic">Alice in Wonderland</em> by Lewis Carroll. These works also fit a category known as juvenile fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">15.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Steampunk fantasy</strong>: This highly specific subgenre combines the Victorian science and technology of the Industrial Revolution with contemporary takes on robots and machines. As such, steampunk fantasy is at once alternate history, science fantasy, and a modern fantasyalthough the specifics vary with specific novels. <em class="mc-text--italic">Soulless</em> by Gail Carriger is a particularly well-regarded steampunk fantasy novel. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">16.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Arthurian fantasy</strong>: These historical fantasy stories exist in a magical world of King Arthur, although Arthur himself is not always the main character. Due to their magical setting, Arthurian fantasy novels and short stories tend to feature mythic creatures like dragons, and many of their heroes are knightswhich also makes them part of the heroic fantasy subgenre. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">17.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Sci-fi fantasy</strong>: These stories can be set in any variety of time periodswhich means they can be a contemporary fantasy, a modern fantasy, a futuristic fantasy, or even historical fantasybut they establish a new world where scientific advancements have changed the rules of engagement, while still incorporating magical elements. The <em class="mc-text--italic">Star Wars</em> series and the various works of Isaac Asimov have helped set the bar for sci-fi fantasy. </li><li class="mc-my-4"> <span class="mc-ml-2">18.</span> <strong class="mc-text--bold">Wuxia fantasy</strong>: This subgenre is rooted in classic Chinese literature. It involves elements of fantasy interspersed with martial arts. <em class="mc-text--italic">Jade City</em> by Fonda Lee is an example of wuxia fantasy. </li></ol></div></div><div class="mc-pb-6 mc-mst-12" id="4iKhu3Oz9NpLTUibeM0gUl"><h2 class="mc-text-h2 highlight-shareable">Want to Learn More About Writing?</h2><div class="mc-text-large mc-mt-4 highlight-shareable"><p class="mc-mb-6">Become a better writer with the <a href='https://www.masterclass.com/' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{"textTag":"p","href":"https://www.masterclass.com/","linkCopy":"Masterclass Annual Membership","category":null}'>Masterclass Annual Membership</a>. Gain access to exclusive video lessons taught by literary masters, including David Baldacci, Joyce Carol Oates, Dan Brown, Margaret Atwood, James Patterson, David Sedaris, and more.</p></div></div></section></div><div class="col-3 d-none d-lg-flex flex-column justify-content-evenly"></div></div></section></div><div id="next-sticky-container" class="bottom 85.2809 29.9444L83.4696 29.4837C80.9034 28.8292 79.712 27.562 79.712 25.5057C79.712 22.9597 81.8134 21.2109 84.7973 21.2109C87.7504 21.2109 89.7749 22.9597 89.843 25.5057H87.7317C87.6053 24.0331 Complete Overview of 18 Fantasy Subgenres","titleTag":"18 Fantasy Subgenres for Writers","author":"MasterClass","description":"\u003cp class=\"mc-mb-6\"\u003eThe broad tent of fantasy literature has Understanding the different fantasy subgenres can help aspiring writers find their niche so that they can create a fantasy series that readers can enjoy for years to come. \u003c/p\u003e","category":{"id":"4DktXg9EiASk9WCkFGQySC","name":"Writing","slug":"writing","featuredArticleId":"nyWbMHzmxicIy6y4uso8m","imageId":"3gxYY24owNfZ4xZegbMVm2","createdAt":"2021-06-07T10:20:31.585-07:00","updatedAt":"2021-06-07T10:20:31.585-07:00","featuredInstructorSlug":"dan-brown"},"instructorSlug":null,"average":"0.0","ratingsCount":0,"updatedAt":"2021-08-06T08:44:47.640-07:00","heroImage":{"id":"4eHYWk9lOVoovZaYsd6EPt","url":"https://images.ctfassets.net/3s5io6mnxfqz/4eHYWk9lOVoovZaYsd6EPt/39dd332a5f875a71d86a371e0db88e63/AdobeStock_295790060.jpeg","contentType":"image/jpeg","title":"a-complete-overview-of-fantasy-subgenres","description":"a-complete-overview-of-fantasy-subgenres","createdAt":"2021-06-07T10:28:07.405-07:00","updatedAt":"2021-06-07T10:28:07.405-07:00"},"creationDate":"2020-01-13T14:37:49.639-08:00","featuredCourseSlug":"dan-brown-teaches-writing-thrillers","mcCategorySlug":"writing","descriptionPlainText":"The broad tent of fantasy literature has spawned many fantasy subgenres that range from mythical and gritty to modern and otherworldly. Understanding the different fantasy subgenres can help aspiring writers find their niche so that they can create a fantasy series that readers can enjoy for years to come. \n","readTime":345,"articleStructuredData":[{"@context":"http://schema.org","@type":"Article","publisher":{"@context":"http://schema.org","@type":"Organization","brand":"MasterClass","name":"MasterClass","url":"http://www.masterclass.com","logo":{"@type":"ImageObject","url":"https://www.masterclass.com/favicon-194x194.png","name":"MasterClass Logo","width":"194","height":"194"},"address":"475 Brannan St Ste 220, San Francisco, CA 94107","email":"support@masterclass.com","contactPoint":[{"@type":"ContactPoint","telephone":"+1 (855) 981-8208","contactType":"customer service"}]},"name":"A Complete Overview of 18 Fantasy Subgenres","headline":"A Complete Overview of 18 Fantasy Subgenres","description":"The broad tent of fantasy literature has spawned many fantasy subgenres that range from mythical and gritty to modern and otherworldly. Understanding the different fantasy subgenres can help aspiring writers find their niche so that they can create a fantasy series that readers can enjoy for years to come. \n","datePublished":"2020-01-13 14:37:49 -0800","dateModified":"2021-08-06 08:44:26 -0700","articleBody":"Fantasy novels take on many forms, and the number of distinct fantasy subgenres seems to grow with each passing year. Here are 18 particularly important subgenres within the world of fantasy:\n\n1. __Dystopian fantasy__: Sometimes grouped in with science fiction, [speculative fiction](https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction), and literary fiction, dystopian fantasies imagine worlds gone wrong. The settings are at once familiar to contemporary audiences and also alarmingly worse than the present world. Jack Vances *Dying Earth* series is a pulpy example of this subgenre of fantasy fiction.\n2. __High fantasy__: Sometimes called epic fantasy, high fantasy is set in a magical environment that has its own rules and physical laws. This subgenres plots and themes have a grand scale and typically center on a single, well-developed hero or a band of heroes, such as Frodo Baggins and his cohorts in J.R.R. Tolkiens *The Lord of the Rings* or Bilbo Baggins and the dwarves in *The Hobbit*. George R.R. Martin combines high fantasy with elements of medieval fantasy and romance in his *Song of Ice and Fire* series (and the *Game of Thrones* television series based upon those books).\n3. __Low fantasy__: Set in the real world, low fantasy includes unexpected magical elements that surprise ordinary characters, like the plastic figurines come to life in Lynne Reid Bankss *The Indian in the Cupboard*.\n4. __Magical realism__: While similar to low fantasy, magical realism characters accept fantastical elements like levitation and telekinesis as a normal part of their otherwise realistic world, as in Gabriel Garca Mrquezs magical realism classic *One Hundred Years of Solitude*.\n5. __Sword and sorcery__: A subset of high fantasy, this subgenre focuses on sword-wielding heroessuch as the titular barbarian in Robert E. Howards *Conan* pulp fiction storiesas well as magic or witchcraft. J.K. Rowling popularized the sword and sorcery subgenre for young adults with her *Harry Potter* series.\n6. __Urban fantasy__: [Urban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories](https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre) in which fantastical characters and concepts are placed in a real world urban setting, often in the present day. Urban fantasy novels have devoted followings and they have spawned film and TV adaptations. Urban fantasy stories often draw from noir and gritty police procedurals. They also may incorporate fantastical elements and supernatural creatures. These could involve undead zombies, vampires, druids, demons, wizardry, witchcraft, and other such fantasy tropes. *The Dresden Files* by Jim Butcher is an example of urban fantasy.\n7. __Paranormal romance__: This fantasy subgenre combines romantic themes with fantasy elements like vampires, werewolves, shifters, faeries, and zombie armies. Many contemporary fantasy series blur the line between urban fantasy stories, coming-of-age tales, and paranormal romances. Patricia Briggs and Jeaniene Frost are popular authors in this subgenre.\n8. __Dark fantasy__: Combining elements of fantasy with the horror genre, dark fantasys aim is to unnerve and frighten readers. For example, consider the gargantuan, [otherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe](https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories). Gothic and Victorian dark fantasy tends to embrace a paranormal setting and supernatural elements, which can range from vampires to werewolves and beyond. Note that by no means is every paranormal fantasy a dark fantasy.\n9. __Grimdark fantasy__: One step beyond dark fantasy, grimdark novels pry into the blackest depths of the human condition, often in the proverbial underbelly of an alternate world. *The Court of Broken Knives* by Anna Smith Spark is a popular book within this subgenre.\n10. __Fables__: Using personified animals and the supernatural, fables impart moral lessons, like the stories in *Aesops Fables* and *Arabian Nights*.\n11. __Fairy Tales__: [Intended for children, fairy tales](https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts) and folk tales are typically set in distant magical worlds (with beginnings like Once upon a time, in a land far, far away) where trolls, dragons, witches, and other supernatural characters are an accepted truth, as in the Brothers Grimms Grimms Fairy Tales.\n12. __Superhero fantasy__: Unlike stories in which a hero acquires special abilities through scientific means, such as exposure to radiation, the protagonists powers in more fantastical superhero stories are supernatural. Many superhero stories are set in a low fantasy worldone thats quite similar to our own world. Superheroes ranging from Wonder Woman to Thor bring fantasy elements to worlds that otherwise obey the known laws of science. Many superhero fantasy authors have worked in the comic book medium, from Stan Lee to Bob Kane. As such, superhero fiction in the fantasy genre is also known as comic fantasy or comic book fantasy.\n13. __Fantasy of manners__: This subgenre, exemplified by fantasy books like *Gormenghast* by Mervyn Peake, combines supernatural world-building with the type of society-centric concerns one might encounter in a work by Edith Wharton or Noel Coward. Human drama and pettiness may outweigh magical powers in this subgenre of fantasy literature.\n14. __Crossworlds fantasy__: Sometimes called portal fantasy, this subgenre involves characters transporting from a normal world to a magical one. This requires authors to engage in both magical world-building and grounded realistic world-building. Crossworlds fantasy stories often appeal to children, as seen in the *Chronicles of Narnia* series by C.S. Lewis and *Alice in Wonderland* by Lewis Carroll. These works also fit a category known as juvenile fantasy.\n15. __Steampunk fantasy__: This highly specific subgenre combines the Victorian science and technology of the Industrial Revolution with contemporary takes on robots and machines. As such, steampunk fantasy is at once alternate history, science fantasy, and a modern fantasyalthough the specifics vary with specific novels. *Soulless* by Gail Carriger is a particularly well-regarded steampunk fantasy novel.\n16. __Arthurian fantasy__: These historical fantasy stories exist in a magical world of King Arthur, although Arthur himself is not always the main character. Due to their magical setting, Arthurian fantasy novels and short stories tend to feature mythic creatures like dragons, and many of their heroes are knightswhich also makes them part of the heroic fantasy subgenre.\n17. __Sci-fi fantasy__: These stories can be set in any variety of time periodswhich means they can be a contemporary fantasy, a modern fantasy, a futuristic fantasy, or even historical fantasybut they establish a new world where scientific advancements have changed the rules of engagement, while still incorporating magical elements. The *Star Wars* series and the various works of Isaac Asimov have helped set the bar for sci-fi fantasy.\n18. __Wuxia fantasy__: This subgenre is rooted in classic Chinese literature. It involves elements of fantasy interspersed with martial arts. *Jade City* by Fonda Lee is an example of wuxia fantasy.\n\nBecome a better writer with the [Masterclass Annual Membership](https://www.masterclass.com/). Gain access to exclusive video lessons taught by literary masters, including David Baldacci, Joyce Carol Oates, Dan Brown, Margaret Atwood, James Patterson, David Sedaris, and more.\nThe broad tent of fantasy literature has spawned many fantasy subgenres that range from mythical and gritty to modern and otherworldly. Understanding the different fantasy subgenres can help aspiring writers find their niche so that they can create a fantasy series that readers can enjoy for years to come. \n","mainEntityOfPage":{"@type":"WebPage","@id":"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/a-complete-overview-of-fantasy-subgenres"},"author":{"@type":"Person","name":"MasterClass"},"image":["https://images.ctfassets.net/3s5io6mnxfqz/4eHYWk9lOVoovZaYsd6EPt/39dd332a5f875a71d86a371e0db88e63/AdobeStock_295790060.jpeg"]}],"articleSubsections":[{"id":"4OwfDU4UkffrE0jncocL3K","title":"18 Common Fantasy Subgenres","videoId":null,"entityType":"subSection","servingSize":null,"cookTime":null,"prepTime":null,"totalTime":null,"calories":null,"recipeCategory":null,"recipeCuisine":null,"recipeYield":null,"keywords":null,"description":"\u003cp class=\"mc-mb-6\"\u003eFantasy novels take on many forms, and the number of distinct fantasy subgenres seems to grow with each passing year. Here are 18 particularly important subgenres within the world of fantasy:\u003c/p\u003e\u003col class=\"mc-m-4\"\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e1.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eDystopian fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Sometimes grouped in with science fiction, \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/what-is-speculative-fiction-defining-and-understanding-the-different-genres-of-speculative-fiction\",\"linkCopy\":\"speculative fiction\",\"category\":null}'\u003especulative fiction\u003c/a\u003e, and literary fiction, dystopian fantasies imagine worlds gone wrong. The settings are at once familiar to contemporary audiences and also alarmingly worse than the present world. Jack Vances \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eDying Earth\u003c/em\u003e series is a pulpy example of this subgenre of fantasy fiction. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e2.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eHigh fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Sometimes called epic fantasy, high fantasy is set in a magical environment that has its own rules and physical laws. This subgenres plots and themes have a grand scale and typically center on a single, well-developed hero or a band of heroes, such as Frodo Baggins and his cohorts in J.R.R. Tolkiens \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Lord of the Rings\u003c/em\u003e or Bilbo Baggins and the dwarves in \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Hobbit\u003c/em\u003e. George R.R. Martin combines high fantasy with elements of medieval fantasy and romance in his \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eSong of Ice and Fire\u003c/em\u003e series (and the \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eGame of Thrones\u003c/em\u003e television series based upon those books). \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e3.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eLow fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Set in the real world, low fantasy includes unexpected magical elements that surprise ordinary characters, like the plastic figurines come to life in Lynne Reid Bankss \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Indian in the Cupboard\u003c/em\u003e. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e4.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eMagical realism\u003c/strong\u003e: While similar to low fantasy, magical realism characters accept fantastical elements like levitation and telekinesis as a normal part of their otherwise realistic world, as in Gabriel Garca Mrquezs magical realism classic \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eOne Hundred Years of Solitude\u003c/em\u003e. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e5.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eSword and sorcery\u003c/strong\u003e: A subset of high fantasy, this subgenre focuses on sword-wielding heroessuch as the titular barbarian in Robert E. Howards \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eConan\u003c/em\u003e pulp fiction storiesas well as magic or witchcraft. J.K. Rowling popularized the sword and sorcery subgenre for young adults with her \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eHarry Potter\u003c/em\u003e series. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e6.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eUrban fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-urban-fantasy-genre\",\"linkCopy\":\"Urban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories\",\"category\":null}'\u003eUrban fantasy is a genre of literature encompassing novels, novellas, and short stories\u003c/a\u003e in which fantastical characters and concepts are placed in a real world urban setting, often in the present day. Urban fantasy novels have devoted followings and they have spawned film and TV adaptations. Urban fantasy stories often draw from noir and gritty police procedurals. They also may incorporate fantastical elements and supernatural creatures. These could involve undead zombies, vampires, druids, demons, wizardry, witchcraft, and other such fantasy tropes. \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Dresden Files\u003c/em\u003e by Jim Butcher is an example of urban fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e7.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eParanormal romance\u003c/strong\u003e: This fantasy subgenre combines romantic themes with fantasy elements like vampires, werewolves, shifters, faeries, and zombie armies. Many contemporary fantasy series blur the line between urban fantasy stories, coming-of-age tales, and paranormal romances. Patricia Briggs and Jeaniene Frost are popular authors in this subgenre. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e8.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eDark fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Combining elements of fantasy with the horror genre, dark fantasys aim is to unnerve and frighten readers. For example, consider the gargantuan, \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/how-to-write-cosmic-horror-stories\",\"linkCopy\":\"otherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe\",\"category\":null}'\u003eotherworldly monsters in H. P. Lovecrafts universe\u003c/a\u003e. Gothic and Victorian dark fantasy tends to embrace a paranormal setting and supernatural elements, which can range from vampires to werewolves and beyond. Note that by no means is every paranormal fantasy a dark fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e9.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eGrimdark fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: One step beyond dark fantasy, grimdark novels pry into the blackest depths of the human condition, often in the proverbial underbelly of an alternate world. \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eThe Court of Broken Knives\u003c/em\u003e by Anna Smith Spark is a popular book within this subgenre. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e10.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eFables\u003c/strong\u003e: Using personified animals and the supernatural, fables impart moral lessons, like the stories in \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eAesops Fables\u003c/em\u003e and \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eArabian Nights\u003c/em\u003e. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e11.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eFairy Tales\u003c/strong\u003e: \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/articles/fairy-tales-vs-folktales-whats-the-difference-plus-fairy-tale-writing-prompts\",\"linkCopy\":\"Intended for children, fairy tales\",\"category\":null}'\u003eIntended for children, fairy tales\u003c/a\u003e and folk tales are typically set in distant magical worlds (with beginnings like Once upon a time, in a land far, far away) where trolls, dragons, witches, and other supernatural characters are an accepted truth, as in the Brothers Grimms Grimms Fairy Tales. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e12.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eSuperhero fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Unlike stories in which a hero acquires special abilities through scientific means, such as exposure to radiation, the protagonists powers in more fantastical superhero stories are supernatural. Many superhero stories are set in a low fantasy worldone thats quite similar to our own world. Superheroes ranging from Wonder Woman to Thor bring fantasy elements to worlds that otherwise obey the known laws of science. Many superhero fantasy authors have worked in the comic book medium, from Stan Lee to Bob Kane. As such, superhero fiction in the fantasy genre is also known as comic fantasy or comic book fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e13.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eFantasy of manners\u003c/strong\u003e: This subgenre, exemplified by fantasy books like \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eGormenghast\u003c/em\u003e by Mervyn Peake, combines supernatural world-building with the type of society-centric concerns one might encounter in a work by Edith Wharton or Noel Coward. Human drama and pettiness may outweigh magical powers in this subgenre of fantasy literature. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e14.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eCrossworlds fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: Sometimes called portal fantasy, this subgenre involves characters transporting from a normal world to a magical one. This requires authors to engage in both magical world-building and grounded realistic world-building. Crossworlds fantasy stories often appeal to children, as seen in the \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eChronicles of Narnia\u003c/em\u003e series by C.S. Lewis and \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eAlice in Wonderland\u003c/em\u003e by Lewis Carroll. These works also fit a category known as juvenile fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e15.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eSteampunk fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: This highly specific subgenre combines the Victorian science and technology of the Industrial Revolution with contemporary takes on robots and machines. As such, steampunk fantasy is at once alternate history, science fantasy, and a modern fantasyalthough the specifics vary with specific novels. \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eSoulless\u003c/em\u003e by Gail Carriger is a particularly well-regarded steampunk fantasy novel. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e16.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eArthurian fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: These historical fantasy stories exist in a magical world of King Arthur, although Arthur himself is not always the main character. Due to their magical setting, Arthurian fantasy novels and short stories tend to feature mythic creatures like dragons, and many of their heroes are knightswhich also makes them part of the heroic fantasy subgenre. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e17.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eSci-fi fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: These stories can be set in any variety of time periodswhich means they can be a contemporary fantasy, a modern fantasy, a futuristic fantasy, or even historical fantasybut they establish a new world where scientific advancements have changed the rules of engagement, while still incorporating magical elements. The \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eStar Wars\u003c/em\u003e series and the various works of Isaac Asimov have helped set the bar for sci-fi fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003cli class=\"mc-my-4\"\u003e \u003cspan class=\"mc-ml-2\"\u003e18.\u003c/span\u003e \u003cstrong class=\"mc-text--bold\"\u003eWuxia fantasy\u003c/strong\u003e: This subgenre is rooted in classic Chinese literature. It involves elements of fantasy interspersed with martial arts. \u003cem class=\"mc-text--italic\"\u003eJade City\u003c/em\u003e by Fonda Lee is an example of wuxia fantasy. \u003c/li\u003e\u003c/ol\u003e","recipeInstructions":null,"review":null,"startTime":null,"brightcoveVideoId":null,"mediaUuid":null,"recipeIngredient":null,"upNextGems":null,"mediaImageUrl":null,"mediaCaption":null},{"id":"4iKhu3Oz9NpLTUibeM0gUl","title":"Want to Learn More About Writing?","videoId":null,"entityType":"subSection","servingSize":null,"cookTime":null,"prepTime":null,"totalTime":null,"calories":null,"recipeCategory":null,"recipeCuisine":null,"recipeYield":null,"keywords":null,"description":"\u003cp class=\"mc-mb-6\"\u003eBecome a better writer with the \u003ca href='https://www.masterclass.com/' target='_blank' class='mc-text--link' data-mc-segment-trigger='true' data-mc-segment-event-type='Article Page Click' data-event-obj='{\"textTag\":\"p\",\"href\":\"https://www.masterclass.com/\",\"linkCopy\":\"Masterclass Annual Membership\",\"category\":null}'\u003eMasterclass Annual Membership\u003c/a\u003e.
